\hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), x, (\beta_x
```
([L_{1}], [R_{1}]), x_{1}, \dots, ([L_{m}], [R_{m}]))
p'_{\mathbf{g}} \leftarrow a_{I\mathbf{g}} \cdot x + a_{O\mathbf{g}} \cdot x^{2} + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{R}) \cdot x + s_{\mathbf{g}} \cdot x^{3}; p'_{u} \leftarrow a_{Iu} \cdot x + a_{Iu} \cdot x^{2} + s_{u} \cdot x^{3} + w\hat{t}
p'_{\mathbf{h}} \leftarrow a_{I\mathbf{h}} \cdot x + a_{O\mathbf{h}} \cdot x^{2} - \mathbf{1}^{n} + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{L}) \cdot x + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{O}) + s_{\mathbf{g}} \cdot x^{3}
         f_{m,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(X) \leftarrow l_{mg_{1+j}} + X^2 + r_{mg_{1+j}}X^{-2} + p_{g_{1+j}}' + \sum_{i=1}^{m-1} (l_{ig_{1+j}}x_i^2 + r_{ig_{1+j}}x_i^{-2})
        f_{m,j}^{\mathbf{h}}(X) \leftarrow l_{mh_{1+j}}X^2 + r_{mh_{1+j}}X^{-2} + p'_{h_{1+j}} + \sum_{i=1}^{m-1} (l_{ih_{1+j}}x_i^2 + r_{ih_{1+j}}x_i^{-2})
f_m^u(X) \leftarrow l_{mu}X^2 + r_{mu}X^{-2} + p'_u + \sum_{i=1}^{m-1} (l_{iu}x_i^2 + r_{iu}x_i^{-2})
 flag ← false
 For t = 1, ..., m - 1 do
          For j = 0, ..., n/2^t - 1 do
                  \mathsf{flag} \leftarrow \mathsf{flag} \vee \mathsf{SZ}(f^{\mathbf{g}}_{m,j}(X) \cdot x^2_t - f^{\mathbf{g}}_{m,j+n/2^t}(X), x_m) \vee \mathsf{SZ}(f^{\mathbf{h}}_{m,j}(X) - f^{\mathbf{h}}_{m,j+n/2^t}(X) \cdot x^2_t, x_m)
For j=0,\ldots,n/2^m-1 do flag \leftarrow flag \vee SZ(f_{m,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(X)\cdot X^2-f_{m,j+n/2^m}^{\mathbf{g}}(X),x_m) \vee SZ(f_{m,j}^{\mathbf{h}}(X)-f_{m,j+n/2^m}^{\mathbf{h}}(X)\cdot X^2,x_m)
\mathsf{flag} \leftarrow \mathsf{flag} \vee \mathsf{SZ} \left( f_m^u(X) - w \cdot \sum_{j=0}^{n/2^m-1} f_{m,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(X) \cdot f_{m,j}^{\mathbf{h}}(X) \cdot y^j, x_m \right)
 Return flag
```

Fig. 13. The function CheckBad function for the ACSPf.

#### **Procedure** $e([\tau])$ :

```
//[\tau] = ((n, Q, \mathbf{g}, \mathbf{h}, u, g, h), (\mathbf{W}_L, \mathbf{W}_R, \mathbf{W}_O, \mathbf{c}); ([A], [S]), (y, z), ([T_1], [T_3], [T_4], [T_5], [T_6]), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), w, ([L_1], [R_1]), x_1, \dots, ([L_{\log n}], [R_{\log n}]), x_{\log n}, (a, b))
Return (a_{I\mathbf{g}}, a_{I\mathbf{h}}, a_{O\mathbf{g}})
```

Fig. 14. The function e for ACSPf.

```
\begin{split} & \frac{\mathbf{Procedure} \, \mathbf{h}([\tau]) \colon}{//[\tau] = \left( (n,Q,\mathbf{g},\mathbf{h},u,g,h), (\mathbf{W}_L,\mathbf{W}_R,\mathbf{W}_O,\mathbf{c}); ([A],[S]), (y,z), ([T_1],[T_3],[T_4],[T_5],[T_6]), x, (\beta_x,\mu,\hat{t}), w, \\ & \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad
```

<span id="page-32-0"></span>**Fig. 15.** The function h for ACSPf.

O(n). Note that ACSPf.V runs in time O(n). Therefore, using Theorem 1, the time complexity of  $\mathcal{E}$  is  $O(q \cdot n)$ .

In order to complete our proof we need to upper bound  $p_{\mathsf{fail}}(\mathsf{ACSPf}, \mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}, \mathsf{e}, R, \lambda)$ . To do so we shall construct an adversary  $\mathcal{H}$  (that runs  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$ ) against that takes as input independent generators  $\mathbf{g}, \mathbf{h}, g, h, u$  of the group  $\mathbb{G}$  and finds a non-trivial discrete logarithm relation between them, i.e., computes  $(e_{\mathbf{g}}, e_{\mathbf{h}}, e_g, e_h, e_u) \neq (\mathbf{0}^n, \mathbf{0}^n, 0, 0, 0)$  such that  $\mathbf{g}^{e_{\mathbf{g}}} \mathbf{h}^{e_h} g^{e_g} h^{e_h} u^{e_u} = 1$ . Then we shall invoke Lemma 2 to transform  $\mathcal{H}$  into an  $\mathcal{F}$  against the discrete logarithm problem.

The adversary  $\mathcal{H}$  has inputs  $\mathbf{g}$ ,  $\mathbf{h}$ , g, h, u, it chooses  $Q \leq 2n$  and runs  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  on public parameters n, Q,  $\mathbf{g}$ ,  $\mathbf{h}$ , g, h, u and simulates the game  $\mathsf{SRS}_{\mathsf{ACSPf}}$  to it. If  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  manages to produce an accepting transcript  $\tau$ ,  $\mathcal{H}$  calls a helper function  $\mathbf{h}$  on input  $[\tau]$  and outputs whatever  $\mathbf{h}$  outputs.

DEFINING h. The function h is defined in Figure 15. It follows from the description of h that it runs time at most O(n). The running time of  $\mathcal H$  consists of the time required to answers q queries, run ACSPf.V in at most q paths in the execution tree and the time required to run h. Hence its time complexity is  $O(q \cdot n)$ . Using Lemma 2, time complexity of  $\mathcal F$  is  $O(q \cdot n)$ .

We shall next discuss the rationale behind the definition of h. Let  $\tau$  be a transcript of ACSPf as shown below.

<span id="page-33-0"></span>
$$\tau = ((n, Q, \mathbf{g}, \mathbf{h}, u, g, h), (\mathbf{W}_L, \mathbf{W}_R, \mathbf{W}_O, \mathbf{c}); (A_I, A_O, S), (y, z), (T_1, T_3, T_4, T_5, T_6), x, (\beta_x, \mu, \hat{t}), w, (L_1, R_1), x_1, (L_2, R_2), x_2, \dots, (L_{\log n}, R_{\log n}), x_{\log n}, (a, b)).$$
(12)

The following equality must hold if  $\tau$  is an accepting transcript.

$$g^{\hat{t}}h^{\beta_x} = g^{x^2(\delta(y,z) + \langle \mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1}, \mathbf{c} \rangle)} T_1^x \cdot \prod_{i=3}^6 T_i^{x^i}$$
.

Writing out  $T_1, T_3, T_4, T_5, T_6$  in terms of their representations and rearranging we shall get that

$$\mathbf{g}^{e_{\mathbf{g}}^{(1)}} \mathbf{h}^{e_{\mathbf{h}}^{(1)}} q^{e_g^{(1)}} h^{e_h^{(1)}} u^{e_u^{(1)}} = 1 ,$$

where  $e_{\mathbf{g}}^{(1)}, e_{\mathbf{h}}^{(1)}, e_{g}^{(1)}, e_{h}^{(1)}, e_{u}^{(1)}$  are as defined in h. Again since  $\tau$  is an accepting transcript the inner product verifier must have returned 1 and hence the following equality must hold.

$$P^{(\log n)} = (\mathbf{g}^{(\log n)})^a (\mathbf{h}^{(\log n)})^b u^{ab}.$$

Now we can write the left hand side of the above equality as

$$\left(\prod_{i=1}^{\log n} L_i^{x_i^2}\right) h^{-\mu} A_I^x \cdot A_O^{x^2} \cdot \mathbf{h}^{-\mathbf{1}^n} \cdot (\mathbf{h}^{\mathbf{y}^{-n}})^{\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_L} \cdot \mathbf{g}^{\mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_R)^x} \cdot (\mathbf{h}^{\mathbf{y}^{-n}})^{\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_O} \cdot S^{x^3} \cdot (u^w)^{\hat{t}} \cdot \left(\prod_{i=1}^{\log n} R_i^{x_i^{-2}}\right) .$$

Let the function bit(k, i, t) return the bit  $k_i$  where  $(k_1, ..., k_t)$  is the t-bit representation of k. Then we can write

$$\mathbf{g}^{(\log n)} = \prod_{k=0}^{n-1} g_{1+k}^{\prod\limits_{i=1}^{\log n} x_i^{(-1)^{1-\mathsf{bit}(k,i,\log n)}}},$$

and

$$\mathbf{h}^{(\log n)} = \prod_{k=0}^{n-1} h_{1+k}^{y^{(-1+k)} \prod_{i=1}^{\log n} x_i^{(-1)^{\mathsf{bit}(k,i,\log n)}}}.$$

Plugging these into the inequality and rearranging we shall get that

$$\mathbf{g}^{e_{\mathbf{g}}^{(2)}} \mathbf{h}^{e_{\mathbf{h}}^{(2)}} g^{e_g^{(2)}} h^{e_h^{(2)}} u^{e_u^{(2)}} = 1 ,$$

where  $e_{\bf g}^{(2)}, e_{\bf h}^{(2)}, e_g^{(2)}, e_h^{(2)}, e_u^{(2)}$  are as defined in h.

Therefore, h always returns a valid discrete logarithm relation when it gets an accepting transcript as input.

RELATING h, e. In order to complete the proof of Theorem 6, in the following lemma we show that – on an accepting transcript  $\tau$  such that  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}^{\mathsf{ACSPf}}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}$  if  $\mathsf{h}([\tau])$  returns a trivial discrete logarithm relation, then  $\mathsf{e}([\tau])$  returns a valid witness.

**Lemma 9.** Let  $\tau$ , as shown in (12), be an accepting transcript of ACSPf such that  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}^{\mathsf{ACSPf}}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}$ . If  $\mathsf{h}([\tau])$  returns  $(\mathbf{0}^n, \mathbf{0}^n, 0, 0, 0, 0)$  then  $\mathsf{e}([\tau])$  returns  $(\mathbf{a}_L^*, \mathbf{a}_R^*, \mathbf{a}_O^*)$  such that

<span id="page-34-0"></span>
$$\mathbf{a}_{L}^{*} \circ \mathbf{a}_{R}^{*} = \mathbf{a}_{O}^{*}$$
 and  $\mathbf{W}_{L} \cdot \mathbf{a}_{L}^{*} + \mathbf{W}_{R} \cdot \mathbf{a}_{R}^{*} + \mathbf{W}_{O} \cdot \mathbf{a}_{O}^{*} = \mathbf{c}$ .

Taking the contrapositive, we have that whenever  $e([\tau])$  fails to extract a valid witness for an accepting transcript  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}^{\mathsf{ACSPf}}$ ,  $\mathsf{h}([\tau])$  outputs a non-trivial discrete logarithm relation, i.e.,  $\mathcal{H}$  succeeds. So we have that

$$p_{\mathsf{fail}}(\mathsf{ACSPf}, \mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}, \mathsf{e}, R, \lambda) \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{dl-rel}}_{\mathbb{G}, 2n+3}(\mathcal{H})$$

Using Lemma 2 we would have that there exists an adversary  $\mathcal{F}$  such that

$$p_{\mathsf{fail}}(\mathsf{ACSPf}, \mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}, \mathsf{e}, R, \lambda) \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{dl}}_{\mathbb{G}}(\mathcal{F}) + \frac{1}{p} \; .$$

Moreover,  $\mathcal{F}$  is nearly as efficient as  $\mathcal{H}$ .

We next prove Lemma 9.

*Proof* (*Lemma 9*). For simplicity let us represent using  $\tau|_c$  the prefix of  $\tau$  just before the challenge c. For example

$$\tau|_{(y,z)} = ((n, Q, \mathbf{g}, \mathbf{h}, u, g, h), (\mathbf{W}_L, \mathbf{W}_R, \mathbf{W}_O, \mathbf{c}), (A_I, A_O, S)).$$

Since  $h([\tau])$  returns  $(\mathbf{0}^n, \mathbf{0}^n, 0, 0, 0)$ , we have that for i = 1, 2

$$(e_{\mathbf{g}}^{(i)}, e_{\mathbf{h}}^{(i)}, e_{q}^{(i)}, e_{h}^{(i)}, e_{u}^{(i)}) = (\mathbf{0}^{n}, \mathbf{0}^{n}, 0, 0, 0)$$
.

Since  $e_g^{(1)} = 0$  we have that  $x^2(\delta(y,z) + \langle \mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1}, \mathbf{c} \rangle) + t_{1g}x + \sum_{i=3}^6 t_{ig}x^i - \hat{t} = 0$ . Hence

<span id="page-34-2"></span>
$$\hat{t} = x^2 (\delta(y, z) + \langle \mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1}, \mathbf{c} \rangle) + t_{1g} x + \sum_{i=3}^{6} t_{ig} x^i .$$
(13)

We define  $p'_{\mathbf{g}}, p'_{\mathbf{h}}, p'_{u}$  as defined in h, i.e.,

$$p'_{\mathbf{g}} = a_{I\mathbf{g}} \cdot x + a_{O\mathbf{g}} \cdot x^{2} + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{R}) \cdot x + s_{\mathbf{g}} \cdot x^{3} ,$$

$$p'_{\mathbf{h}} = a_{I\mathbf{h}} \cdot x + a_{O\mathbf{h}} \cdot x^{2} - \mathbf{1}^{n} + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{L}) \cdot x + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{O}) + s_{\mathbf{g}} \cdot x^{3} ,$$

$$p'_{u} = a_{Iu} \cdot x + a_{Iu} \cdot x^{2} + s_{u} \cdot x^{3} + w\hat{t} .$$

Since  $e_{\mathbf{g}}^{(2)} = \mathbf{0}^n$ , we have that for all  $k \in \{0, \dots, n-1\}$ 

<span id="page-34-1"></span>
$$\left(\sum_{i=1}^{\log n} (l_{ig_{1+k}} x_i^2 + r_{ig_{1+k}} x_i^{-2}) + p'_{g_{1+k}}\right) - a \cdot \left(\prod_{i=1}^{\log n} x_i^{(-1)^{1-\operatorname{bit}(k,i,\log n)}}\right) = 0.$$
(14)

We also have  $e_{\mathbf{h}}^{(2)} = \mathbf{0}^n$ , i.e., for all  $k \in \{0, ..., n-1\}$ 

$$\left(\sum_{i=1}^{\log n} (l_{ih_{1+k}} x_i^2 + r_{ih_{1+k}} x_i^{-2}) + p'_{h_{1+k}}\right) - by^{(-(k))} \cdot \left(\prod_{i=1}^{\log n} x_i^{(-1)^{\mathsf{bit}(k,i,\log n)}}\right) = 0.$$
 (15)

From  $e_u^{(2)} = 0$  we have that

<span id="page-35-1"></span><span id="page-35-0"></span>
$$\left(\sum_{i=1}^{\log n} (l_{iu}x_i^2 + r_{iu}x_i^{-2})\right) + p_u' - w \cdot ab = 0.$$
 (16)

We shall next use the following lemma which essentially says that if none of  $e_{\mathbf{g}}^{(2)}, e_{\mathbf{h}}^{(2)}, e_{u}^{(2)}, e_{g}^{(2)}, e_{h}^{(2)}$  are non-zero and  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}^{\mathsf{ACSPf}}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}$ , then  $w \cdot \langle p'_{\mathbf{g}}, p'_{\mathbf{h}} \circ \mathbf{y}^n \rangle = p'_u$ . It is very similar to Lemma 7 that we encountered in the analysis of RngPf. This similarity is due to both ACSPf and RngPf use the inner-product argument.

The equalities in the statement of this lemma hold if the inner-product argument verifier accepts and the discrete logarithm problem is hard in group  $\mathbb{G}$ . The lemma shows that if none of the challenges in the inner-product argument were bad, then the inner-product of the vectors  $p'_{\mathbf{g}}$  and  $p'_{\mathbf{h}} \circ \mathbf{y}^n$  is  $p'_u/w$ . This is a generalization of the proof that we saw in the technical overview where we analysed the inner-product argument for n=2.

**Lemma 10.** Let  $\tau$ , as shown in (12), be an accepting transcript of ACSPf such that  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}^{\mathsf{ACSPf}}$ . Let

$$p'_{\mathbf{g}} = a_{I\mathbf{g}} \cdot x + a_{O\mathbf{g}} \cdot x^{2} + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{R}) \cdot x + s_{\mathbf{g}} \cdot x^{3} ,$$

$$p'_{\mathbf{h}} = a_{I\mathbf{h}} \cdot x + a_{O\mathbf{h}} \cdot x^{2} - \mathbf{1}^{n} + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{L}) \cdot x + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{O}) + s_{\mathbf{g}} \cdot x^{3} ,$$

$$p'_{\mathbf{u}} = a_{I\mathbf{u}} \cdot x + a_{I\mathbf{u}} \cdot x^{2} + s_{\mathbf{u}} \cdot x^{3} + w\hat{t} .$$

Suppose, the for all  $k \in \{0, ..., n-1\}$ 

$$\left(\sum_{i=1}^{\log n} (l_{ig_{1+k}} x_i^2 + r_{ig_{1+k}} x_i^{-2}) + p_{g_{1+k}}'\right) - a \cdot \left(\prod_{i=1}^{\log n} x_i^{(-1)^{1-\operatorname{bit}(k,i,\log n)}}\right) = 0 \;,$$

$$\left(\sum_{i=1}^{\log n} (l_{ih_{1+k}} x_i^2 + r_{ih_{1+k}} x_i^{-2}) + p'_{h_{1+k}}\right) - by^{(-(k))} \cdot \left(\prod_{i=1}^{\log n} x_i^{(-1)^{\mathsf{bit}(k,i,\log n)}}\right) = 0.$$

Additionally,

$$\left(\sum_{i=1}^{\log n} (l_{iu}x_i^2 + r_{iu}x_i^{-2})\right) + p_u' - w \cdot ab = 0.$$
(17)

Then

$$w \cdot \langle p'_{\mathbf{g}}, p'_{\mathbf{h}} \circ \mathbf{y}^n \rangle = p'_u$$
.

*Proof* (*Lemma* 10). We shall invoke Lemma 8 to prove this lemma. Let

$$\mathsf{params} = \left\{ \{l_{i\mathbf{g}}, l_{i\mathbf{h}}, l_{iu}, r_{i\mathbf{g}}, r_{i\mathbf{h}}, r_{iu}\}_{i=1}^{\log n}, p_{\mathbf{g}}', p_{\mathbf{h}}', p_{u}' \right\} \ .$$

Consider the function Bad defined in Figure 11. Note that since Bad(params, x, j) returns true if and only if  $x \in \text{BadCh}(\tau|_{x_j})$ ,  $x_1, \ldots, x_{\log n}$  in  $\tau$  satisfy the condition for  $x_i$ 's in Lemma 8. Moreover all the equalities required in Lemma 8 hold and  $p'_{\mathbf{g}}, p'_{\mathbf{h}}, p'_{\mathbf{u}} \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ . So we using Lemma 8 we have that

$$w \cdot \langle p'_{\mathbf{g}}, p'_{\mathbf{h}} \circ \mathbf{y}^n \rangle = p'_u$$
.

Since  $\tau$  is an accepting transcript of ACSPf and  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}^{\mathsf{ACSPf}}$  and (14) to (16) hold, using Lemma 10, we get

$$w\langle p'_{\mathbf{g}}, p'_{\mathbf{h}} \circ \mathbf{y}^n \rangle = p'_u$$
.

Plugging in the values of  $p'_{\mathbf{g}}, p'_{\mathbf{h}}, p'_{u}$  we get

$$w \cdot \left\langle \left( a_{I\mathbf{g}}x + a_{O\mathbf{g}}x^2 + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_R) x + s_{\mathbf{g}}x^3 \right), \mathbf{y}^n \circ \left( a_{I\mathbf{h}}x + a_{O\mathbf{h}}x^2 - \mathbf{1}^n + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_L) \cdot x + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_O) + s_{\mathbf{g}}x^3 \right) \right\rangle = a_{Iu}x + a_{Iu}x^2 + s_{u}x^3 + w\hat{t}.$$

Since  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}^{\mathsf{ACSPf}}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}$ , we have that  $w \notin \mathsf{BadCh}(\tau|_w)$ . Therefore,  $\mathsf{SZ}(f(W), w)$  is false where f is as defined in  $\mathsf{CheckBad}(\tau', w)$ . Since we have here that f(w) = 0, the polynomial f(W) must be the zero polynomial. In particular its W term must be zero, i.e.,

$$\hat{t} = \left\langle \left( a_{I\mathbf{g}}x + a_{O\mathbf{g}}x^2 + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_R)x + s_{\mathbf{g}}x^3 \right),$$

$$\mathbf{y}^n \circ \left( a_{I\mathbf{h}}x + a_{O\mathbf{h}}x^2 - \mathbf{1}^n + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_L)x + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_O) + s_{\mathbf{g}}x^3 \right) \right\rangle.$$

Plugging in the value of  $\hat{t}$  obtained in (13), we have that

$$x^{2}(\delta(y,z) + \langle \mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1}, \mathbf{c} \rangle) + t_{1g}x + \sum_{i=3}^{6} t_{ig}x^{i} - \left\langle a_{I\mathbf{g}}x + a_{O\mathbf{g}}x^{2} + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{R})x + s_{\mathbf{g}}x^{3}, \right.$$
$$\mathbf{y}^{n} \circ \left( a_{I\mathbf{h}}x + a_{O\mathbf{h}}x^{2} - \mathbf{1}^{n} + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{L})x + \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{O}) + s_{\mathbf{g}}x^{3} \right) \right\rangle = 0.$$

Since  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}^{\mathsf{ACSPf}}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}$ , we have that  $x \notin \mathsf{BadCh}(\tau|_x)$ . Therefore,  $\mathsf{SZ}(f_4(X),x)$  is false where  $f_4$  is as defined in  $\mathsf{CheckBad}(\tau',x)$ . Since we have here that  $f_4(x)=0$ , the polynomial  $f_4(X)$  must be the zero polynomial. In particular its  $X^2$  term must be zero, i.e.,

$$\begin{split} &\delta(y,z) + \langle \mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1}, \mathbf{c} \rangle - \langle a_{I\mathbf{g}}, \mathbf{y}^n \circ a_{I\mathbf{h}} \rangle - \langle a_{I\mathbf{g}}, \mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_L \rangle + \langle a_{O\mathbf{g}}, \mathbf{y}^n \rangle \\ &- \langle \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_R), \mathbf{y}^n \circ a_{I\mathbf{h}} \rangle - \langle \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_R), (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_L) \rangle = 0 \ . \end{split}$$

Plugging in  $\delta(y,z) = \langle \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_R), (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_L) \rangle$ , we get

$$\langle \mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1}, \mathbf{c} \rangle - \langle a_{I\mathbf{g}}, \mathbf{y}^{n} \circ a_{I\mathbf{h}} \rangle - \langle a_{I\mathbf{g}}, \mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{L} \rangle + \langle a_{O\mathbf{g}}, \mathbf{y}^{n} \rangle - \langle \mathbf{y}^{-n} \circ (\mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{R}), \mathbf{y}^{n} \circ a_{I\mathbf{h}} \rangle - \langle a_{O\mathbf{g}}, \mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1} \cdot \mathbf{W}_{O} \rangle = 0.$$

Simplifying and rearranging we get

$$\langle \mathbf{z}_{[1:]}^{Q+1}, \mathbf{c} - \mathbf{W}_L \cdot a_{I\mathbf{g}} - \mathbf{W}_R \cdot a_{I\mathbf{h}} - \mathbf{W}_O \cdot a_{O\mathbf{g}} \rangle - \langle a_{I\mathbf{g}} \circ a_{I\mathbf{h}} - a_{O\mathbf{g}}, \mathbf{y}^n \rangle = 0$$
.

Since  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}^{\mathsf{ACSPf}}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}$ , we have that  $(y,z) \notin \mathsf{BadCh}(\tau|_{(y,z)})$ . Therefore,  $\mathsf{SZ}(f(Y,Z),(y,z))$  is false where f is as defined in  $\mathsf{CheckBad}(\tau',(y,z))$ . Since we have here that f(y,z)=0, the polynomial f(Y,Z) is the vector polynomial. Equating all its coefficients to zero, we get

$$\mathbf{W}_L \cdot a_{I\mathbf{g}} + \mathbf{W}_R \cdot a_{I\mathbf{h}} + \mathbf{W}_O \cdot a_{O\mathbf{g}} = \mathbf{c} , a_{I\mathbf{g}} \circ a_{I\mathbf{h}} = a_{O\mathbf{g}} .$$

Since  $(\mathbf{a}_L^*, \mathbf{a}_R^*, \mathbf{a}_O^*)$  returned by e is  $(a_{I\mathbf{g}}, a_{I\mathbf{h}}, a_{O\mathbf{g}})$  we have that

$$\mathbf{a}_L^* \circ \mathbf{a}_R^* = \mathbf{a}_O^*$$
 and  $\mathbf{W}_L \cdot \mathbf{a}_L^* + \mathbf{W}_R \cdot \mathbf{a}_R^* + \mathbf{W}_O \cdot \mathbf{a}_O^* = \mathbf{c}$ .

#### <span id="page-37-0"></span>5.4 Proof of Lemma 8

From the statement of the algebraic lemma, it is evident that we need to eliminate everything except for  $p'_{\mathbf{g}}, p'_{\mathbf{h}}, y, p'_{u}, w$  to obtain a relation between them. Our first step would be to plug in the values of a, b from the first two sets of equalities into the third – this would eliminate a, b. Then we shall exploit the first two sets of equalities and the definition of Bad to arrive at an equation solely in terms of  $p'_{\mathbf{g}}, p'_{\mathbf{h}}, y, p'_{u}, w$ .

Proof (Lemma 8).

First we observe that given that  $\mathsf{Bad}(\mathsf{params}, x, j) \neq \mathsf{true}$ , if for any of the polynomials p(X) on which SZ is called in  $\mathsf{Bad}$ , p(x) is zero, then the polynomial p(X) is the zero polynomial. We shall use this observation repeatedly in this proof.

SIMPLIFYING NOTATION. We introduce some new notation for simplicity. We define the following polynomials. For all  $k \in \{1, ..., \log n\}$ , for all  $j \in \{0, ..., n-1\}$ 

$$f_{k,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(X) = l_{kg_{1+j}}X^{2} + r_{kg_{1+j}}X^{-2} + p'_{g_{1+j}} + \sum_{i=1}^{k-1} (l_{ig_{1+j}}x_{i}^{2} + r_{ig_{1+j}}x_{i}^{-2}),$$

$$f_{k,j}^{\mathbf{h}}(X) = l_{kh_{1+j}}X^{2} + r_{kh_{1+j}}X^{-2} + p'_{h_{1+j}} + \sum_{i=1}^{k-1} (l_{ih_{1+j}}x_{i}^{2} + r_{ih_{1+j}}x_{i}^{-2}).$$
(18)

<span id="page-37-1"></span>For all  $k \in \{1, \ldots, \log n\}$ 

<span id="page-37-2"></span>
$$f_k^u(X) = l_{ku}X^2 + r_{ku}X^{-2} + p_u' + \sum_{i=1}^{k-1} (l_{iu}x_i^2 + r_{iu}x_i^{-2}).$$
(19)

Using our notation in (18) and (19), we can re-write our given equalities as

1. for  $k = 0, \ldots, n-1$ 

$$a = f_{\log n, k}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n}) \cdot \left( \prod_{i=1}^{\log n} x_i^{(-1)^{\mathsf{bit}(k, i, \log n)}} \right) .$$

2. for  $k = 0, \ldots, n - 1$ 

$$b = f_{\log n,k}^{\mathbf{h}}(x_{\log n}) \cdot y^{((k))} \cdot \left( \prod_{i=1}^{\log n} x_i^{(-1)^{1-\mathsf{bit}(k,i,\log n)}} \right) .$$

3.

$$f_{\log n}^u(x_{\log n}) - w \cdot ab = 0.$$

ELIMINATING a, b IN THE THIRD EQUALITY. First off, we plug the values of a, b we obtain for k = 0 into the third equality. We obtain

<span id="page-38-0"></span>
$$f_{\log n}^{u}(x_{\log n}) - w \cdot f_{\log n,1}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n}) \cdot f_{\log n,1}^{\mathbf{h}}(x_{\log n}) = 0$$
 (20)

In order to eliminate all variable except  $p'_{\mathbf{g}}, p'_{\mathbf{h}}, y, p'_{u}, w$ , we need to use the first two sets of equalities to obtain relations that we can plug back into (20).

RELATIONS FROM THE FIRST SET OF EQUALITIES. The first set of equalities gave us that for  $k=0,\ldots,n-1$ 

$$a = f_{\log n,k}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n}) \cdot \left(\prod_{i=1}^{\log n} x_i^{(-1)^{\mathsf{bit}(k,i,\log n)}}\right) . \tag{21}$$

Let  $t \in \{1, ..., \log n\}$  and  $j \in \{0, ..., n/2^t - 1\}$ . Equating the values of a for k = j and  $k = j + n/2^t$ , we get

$$f_{\log n,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n}) \cdot \left(\prod_{i=1}^{\log n} x_i^{(-1)^{\mathsf{bit}(j,i,\log n)}}\right) = f_{\log n,j+n/2^t}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n}) \cdot \left(\prod_{i=1}^{\log n} x_i^{(-1)^{\mathsf{bit}(j+n/2^t,i,\log n)}}\right) \ .$$

Since  $j \in \{0, \dots, n/2^t - 1\}$ , j and  $j + n/2^t$  differ only in the  $t^{\text{th}}$  bit. So, we have for  $t \in \{1, \dots, \log n\}$ ,  $j \in \{0, \dots, n/2^t - 1\}$ 

$$f_{\log n, j}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n}) \cdot x_t^2 = f_{\log n, j + n/2^t}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n})$$
 (22)

We shall next show that for all  $t \in \{1, ..., \log n\}$ , for all  $j \in \{0, ..., n/2^t - 1\}$ 

$$l_{tg_{1+j}} = 0, r_{tg_{1+j}} = f_{t-1,j+n/2^t}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{t-1}).$$

First we show it for  $t = \log n$ - in this case j can take the value only 0. We have that

$$f_{\log n,0}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n}) \cdot x_{\log n}^2 - f_{\log n,1}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n}) = 0$$
.

Since Bad(params,  $x_{\log n}$ ,  $\log n$ ) = false

$$f_{\log n,0}^{\mathbf{g}}(X) \cdot X^2 - f_{\log n,1}^{\mathbf{g}}(X)$$

is the zero polynomial. Equating the constant term to 0 we get

$$r_{(\log n)g_1} = f_{\log n - 1, 1}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n - 1}),$$

Equating the  $X^4$  term to 0 we get,

$$l_{(\log n)q_1} = 0.$$

Hence, it holds for  $t = \log n$ . Now let  $t = t' < \log n$ . We have that for  $j \in \{0, \dots, n/2^{t'} - 1\}$ .

$$f_{\log n,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n}) \cdot x_{t'}^{2} - f_{\log n,j+n/2t'}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n}) = 0$$
.

Since Bad(params,  $x_{\log n}$ ,  $\log n$ ) = false

$$f_{\log n,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(X) \cdot x_{t'}^2 - f_{\log n,j+n/2t'}^{\mathbf{g}}(X)$$

is the zero polynomial. Therefore, its constant term is 0, i.e.,

$$f_{\log n-1,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n-1}) \cdot x_{t'}^2 - f_{\log n,j+n/2t'}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{\log n-1}) = 0$$
.

Using similar series of arguments (since for all  $j \in \{\log n - 1, \log n - 2, \dots, t'\}$ : Bad(params,  $x_j, j$ ) = false) we can arrive at

$$f_{t',j}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{t'}) \cdot x_{t'}^2 - f_{t',j+n/2t'}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{t'}) = 0$$
.

Now, since Bad(params,  $x'_t, t'$ ) = false

$$f_{t',j}^{\mathbf{g}}(X) \cdot X^2 - f_{t',j+n/2^{t'}}^{\mathbf{g}}(X)$$

must be the zero polynomial. Equating the constant term to 0 we get for t' > 1

$$r_{t'g_j} = f_{t'-1,j+n/2^{t'}}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{t'-1}),$$

and for t' = 1

$$r_{1g_{1+j}} = p'_{g_{1+j+n/2}}$$
.

Equating the  $X^4$  term to 0 we get,

$$l_{t'q_i}=0$$
.

Hence for all  $t \in \{2, \dots, \log n\}$ , for all  $j \in \{0, \dots, n/2^t - 1\}$ 

<span id="page-39-0"></span>
$$l_{tg_{1+j}} = 0, r_{tg_{1+j}} = f_{t-1, j+n/2t}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{t-1}),$$
 (23)

and for all  $j \in \{0, ..., n/2 - 1\}$ 

<span id="page-39-2"></span>
$$r_{1g_{1+j}} = p'_{g_{1+j+n/2}}, l_{1g_{1+j}} = 0.$$
 (24)

RELATIONS FROM THE SECOND SET OF EQUALITIES. Now, we can go through an identical process for the second set of equalities and obtain that (we omit the calculations since they are identical to the ones we saw previously)

1. for all  $t \in \{2, ..., \log n\}$ , for all  $j \in \{0, ..., n/2^t - 1\}$ 

<span id="page-39-1"></span>
$$r_{th_{1+j}} = 0 , l_{th_{1+j}} = f_{t-1,j+n/2^t}^{\mathbf{h}}(x_t) \cdot y^{n/2^t} .$$
 (25)

2. for all  $j \in \{0, \dots, n/2 - 1\}$ 

<span id="page-39-3"></span>
$$r_{1h_{1+j}} = 0, l_{1h_{1+j}} = p'_{h_{1+j+n/2}} \cdot y^{n/2}.$$
 (26)

PUTTING IT ALL TOGETHER. Finally, we are ready to use the obtained relations. We shall show using induction on k that for all  $k \in \{1, ..., \log n\}$ 

$$f_k^u(x_k) - w \cdot \sum_{j=0}^{n/2^k - 1} f_{k,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_k) \cdot f_{k,j}^{\mathbf{h}}(x_k) \cdot y^j = 0$$
.

The base case for  $k = \log n$  is true since (20) holds.

Now assuming it holds for some k = k' we shall show that it holds for k' - 1 as well. Using induction hypothesis we have that

$$f_{k'}^{u}(x_{k'}) - w \cdot \sum_{j=0}^{n/2^{k'}-1} f_{k',j}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{k'}) \cdot f_{k',j}^{\mathbf{h}}(x_{k'}) \cdot y^{j} = 0$$
.

Since  $\mathsf{Bad}(\mathsf{params}, x_k', k') \neq \mathsf{true}$ , the polynomial

$$f_{k'}^{u}(X) - w \cdot \sum_{j=0}^{n/2^{k'}-1} f_{k',j}^{\mathbf{g}}(X) \cdot f_{k',j}^{\mathbf{h}}(X) \cdot y^{j}$$

must be the zero polynomial, i.e., in particular its constant term is zero. It's constant term can be written as

$$f_{k'-1}^{u}(x_{k'-1}) - w \cdot \sum_{j=0}^{n/2^{k'}-1} f_{k'-1,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{k'-1}) \cdot f_{k'-1,j}^{\mathbf{h}}(x_{k'-1}) \cdot y^{j} - w \cdot \sum_{j=0}^{n/2^{k'}-1} (l_{k'g_{1+j}} \cdot r_{k'h_{1+j}} + r_{k'g_{1+j}} \cdot l_{k'h_{1+j}}) \cdot y^{j}).$$

From (23) and (25) we have that for  $j \in \{0,\dots,n/2^{k'}-1\}$ 

$$r_{k'g_{1+j}} = f_{k'-1,j+n/2^{k'}}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{k'-1}) , \ l_{k'g_{1+j}} = 0 , \ r_{k'h_{1+j}} = 0 , \ l_{k'h_{1+j}} = f_{k'-1,j+n/2^{k'}}^{\mathbf{h}}(x_{k'-1}) \cdot y^{n/2^{k'}} .$$

So, equating the constant term to 0 we have that

$$f_{k'-1}^{u}(x_{k'-1}) - w \cdot \sum_{j=0}^{n/2^{k'}-1} (f_{k'-1,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{k'-1}) \cdot f_{k'-1,j}^{\mathbf{h}}(x_{k'-1}) \cdot y^{j})$$
$$- w \cdot \sum_{j=0}^{n/2^{k'}-1} ((f_{k'-1,j+n/2^{k'}}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{k'-1}) \cdot f_{k'-1,j+n/2^{k'}}^{\mathbf{h}}(x_{k'-1})) \cdot y^{j+n/2^{k'}}) = 0.$$

This can be simplified to

$$f_{k'-1}^{u}(x_{k'-1}) - w \cdot \sum_{j=0}^{n/2^{k'-1}-1} (f_{k'-1,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_{k'-1}) \cdot f_{k'-1,j}^{\mathbf{h}}(x_{k'-1}) \cdot y^{j} = 0.$$

Hence we have shown that it holds for k = k' - 1. Hence, by induction we arrive at

$$f_1^u(x_1) - w \cdot \sum_{j=0}^{n/2-1} (f_{1,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(x_1) \cdot f_{1,j}^{\mathbf{h}}(x_1) \cdot y^j = 0.$$

Since Bad(params,  $x'_k, k'$ )  $\neq$  true, the polynomial

$$f_1^u(X) - w \cdot \sum_{j=0}^{n/2-1} (f_{1,j}^{\mathbf{g}}(X) \cdot f_{1,j}^{\mathbf{h}}(X) \cdot y^j)$$

is the zero polynomial, i.e., in particular its constant term is 0. So, we have that

$$p'_{u} - w \sum_{j=0}^{n/2-1} p'_{g_{1+j}} \cdot p'_{h_{1+j}} \cdot y^{j} - w \sum_{j=0}^{n/2-1} (l_{1g_{1+j}} \cdot r_{1h_{1+j}} + r_{1g_{1+j}} \cdot l_{1h_{1+j}}) \cdot y^{j} = 0.$$

From (24) and (26) we have that for  $j \in \{0, ..., n/2 - 1\}$ 

$$r_{1g_{1+j}} = p'_{g_{1+j+n/2}}, l_{1g_{1+j}} = 0, r_{1h_{1+j}} = 0, l_{1h_{1+j}} = p'_{h_{1+j+n/2}} \cdot y^{n/2}$$

So, we have that

$$p'_{u} - w \sum_{j=0}^{n/2-1} p'_{g_{1+j}} \cdot p'_{h_{1+j}} \cdot y^{j} - w \sum_{j=0}^{n/2-1} (l_{1g_{1+j}} \cdot r_{1h_{1+j}} + r_{1g_{1+j}} \cdot l_{1h_{1+j}} \cdot y^{n/2}) \cdot y^{j} = 0.$$

Simplifying we get that

$$p'_u = w \cdot \langle p'_{\mathbf{g}}, p'_{\mathbf{h}} \circ \mathbf{y}^n \rangle$$
.

#### 6 Online srs-wee Security of Sonic

We apply our framework to prove srs-wee security of Sonic [18] which is an interactive argument for arithmetic circuit satisfiability based on pairings (we refer to this argument as SnACSPf). The argument SnACSPf is again an argument of knowledge for the relation (11). Sonic represents arithmetic circuits using the same constraint system as the one used in Bulletproofs. The constraint system has three vectors  $\mathbf{a}_L, \mathbf{a}_R, \mathbf{a}_O \in \mathbb{Z}_p^n$  representing the left inputs, right inputs, and outputs of multiplication gates respectively, so that  $\mathbf{a}_L \circ \mathbf{a}_R = \mathbf{a}_O$ , with additional  $Q \leq 2n$  linear constraints. The linear constraints can be represented as  $\mathbf{a}_L \cdot \mathbf{W}_L + \mathbf{a}_R \cdot \mathbf{W}_R + \mathbf{a}_O \cdot \mathbf{W}_O = \mathbf{c}$ , where  $\mathbf{W}_L, \mathbf{W}_R, \mathbf{W}_O \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{Q \times n}$ .

PAIRINGS. As stated before, SnACSPf is based on pairings. Let  $\mathbb{G}_1, \mathbb{G}_2, \mathbb{G}_T$  be groups of prime order p with generators  $g \in \mathbb{G}_1, h \in \mathbb{G}_2$ . A pairing is a bilinear map  $e : \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 \to \mathbb{G}_T$  such that  $e(g^a, h^b) = e(g, h)^{ab}$  for all  $a, b \in \mathbb{Z}_p$  and e(g, h) is a generator of  $\mathbb{G}_T$ . In our AGM analysis, we shall consider symmetric pairings, i.e.,  $\mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}$ . We shall assume that SnACSPf  $= \mathbb{S}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_2 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_2 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_2 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 = \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1 \times \mathbb{G}_1$ 

The interactive argument SnACSPf. is a argument of knowledge for the following relation.

$$R = \{ (((n, Q \in \mathbb{N}^+), (\mathbf{W}_L, \mathbf{W}_R, \mathbf{W}_O \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{Q \times n}, \mathbf{c} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^Q)), (\mathbf{a}_L, \mathbf{a}_R, \mathbf{a}_O \in \mathbb{Z}_p^n) \} : \mathbf{a}_L \circ \mathbf{a}_R = \mathbf{a}_O \wedge \mathbf{W}_L \cdot \mathbf{a}_L + \mathbf{W}_R \cdot \mathbf{a}_R + \mathbf{W}_O \cdot \mathbf{a}_O = \mathbf{c} \} .$$

The setup algorithm SnACSPf.Setup fixes an integer d such that 4n > d > 3n. It generates the bilinear parameters bp =  $((p, \mathbb{G}, \mathbb{G}_T, e, g, h))$ . It then samples  $\alpha, x$  uniformly at random from  $\mathbb{Z}_p$ . It sets

$$\mathrm{srs} = \{g, \{g^{x^i}\}_{i=-d}^d, \{h^{x^i}\}_{i=-d}^d, \{h^{\alpha x^i}\}_{i=-d}^d, \{g^{\alpha x^i}\}_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d, e(g,h^\alpha)\} \;.$$

It returns (bp, srs) as its output.

As shown in [18] the argument for the above relation proceeds by defining following polynomials r(X,Y), k(Y), s(X,Y), t(X,Y) and proving that the constant term of t(X,Y) is zero.

$$\begin{split} & r(X,Y) \leftarrow \left\langle \mathbf{a}_{L}, \mathbf{X}_{[1:]}^{n+1} \circ \mathbf{Y}_{[1:]}^{n+1} \right\rangle + \left\langle \mathbf{a}_{R}, \mathbf{X}_{[1:]}^{-n-1} \circ \mathbf{Y}_{[1:]}^{n+1} \right\rangle + \left\langle \mathbf{a}_{O}, \mathbf{X}_{[n+1:]}^{-2n-1} \circ \mathbf{Y}_{[n+1:]}^{-2n-1} \right\rangle, \\ & k(Y) \leftarrow \left\langle \mathbf{c}, \mathbf{Y}_{[n+1:]}^{Q+n+1} \right\rangle, \\ & s(X,Y) \leftarrow \mathbf{Y}_{[n+1:]}^{Q+n+1} \cdot \left( \mathbf{W}_{L} \cdot \mathbf{X}_{[1:]}^{-n-1} + \mathbf{W}_{R} \cdot \mathbf{X}_{[1:]}^{n+1} + \mathbf{W}_{O} \cdot \mathbf{X}_{[n+1:]}^{2n+1} \right) + \left\langle -\mathbf{Y}_{[1:]}^{n+1} - \mathbf{Y}_{[1:]}^{-n-1}, \mathbf{X}_{[n+1:]}^{2n+1} \right\rangle, \\ & t(X,Y) \leftarrow r(X,1)(r(X,Y) + s(X,Y)) - k(Y) \;. \end{split}$$

Note that the verifier can evaluate s(X,Y), k(Y) without the witness. However evaluating s(X,Y) is expensive, hence the prover the prover computes the value and the prover and the verifier engage in an argument for signature of correct computation where the prover demonstrates to the verifier that it sent the correct evaluation. This argument for signature of correct computation assumes that the polynomial s(X,Y) can be expressed as a sum of M polynomials of the form  $\psi_j(X,Y) = \sum_{i=1}^n \psi_{j,\sigma_{j,i}} X^i Y^{\sigma_{j,i}}$  where  $\sigma_j = (\sigma_{j,1},\ldots,\sigma_{j,n})$  is a permutation of  $(1,\ldots,n)$ . As stated in [18], for any given arithmetic circuit, one can devise a constraint system such that s(X,Y) can be represented as a sum of M=O(1) such polynomials.

The prover and the verifier algorithms, SnACSPf.P, SnACSPf.V are shown in Figure 16 with all sub-components defined in Figures 17 to 21. The complexity of the protocol necessitates this modular description. Figure 17 describes the polynomial commitments used in Sonic and Figure 18 describes the signature of correct computation which uses the polynomial permutation argument defined in Figure 19 which in turn uses the grand product argument in Figure 20. The argument for well-formedness of commitments used by the grand product argument is defined in Figure 21.

In the soundness analysis of SnACSPf in [18], only the bounded polynomial extractibility and evaluation binding of the commitment scheme is analysed in the AGM.<sup>6</sup> Here we give an analysis of the srs-wee of SnACSPf in the AGM.

<span id="page-42-1"></span>We prove the following theorem that establishes an upper bound on the advantage against online srs-wee security of SnACSPf.

**Theorem 7.** Let  $\mathbb{G} = \{\mathbb{G}_{\lambda}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}^+}$  be a family of groups with order  $p = p(\lambda)$ . Let  $\mathbb{G}_T = \{\mathbb{G}_{T,\lambda}\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}^+}$  be a family of groups such that there exists a bilinear map  $e : \mathbb{G} \times \mathbb{G} \to \mathbb{G}_T$ . Let  $\mathsf{SnACSPf} = \mathsf{SnACSPf}[\mathbb{G}, \mathbb{G}_T, e]$  be the interactive argument system as described in Figure 16, for the relation R in (11). We can construct an extractor  $\mathcal{E}$  such that for any non-uniform algebraic prover  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  making at most  $q = q(\lambda)$  queries to its oracle, there exist non-uniform adversaries  $\mathcal{F}_1, \mathcal{F}_2, \mathcal{F}_3$  with the property that for any (computationally unbounded) distinguisher  $\mathcal{D}$ , for all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}^+$ ,

$$\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{sr\text{-}wee}}_{\mathsf{SnACSPf},R}(\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}},\mathcal{D},\mathcal{E},\lambda) \leqslant \frac{18nq}{p-1} + \mathsf{Adv}^{4n\text{-}\mathsf{dl}}_{\mathbb{G}}(\mathcal{F}_1,\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{dl}}_{\mathbb{G}}(\mathcal{F}_2,\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{dl}}_{\mathbb{G}}(\mathcal{F}_3,\lambda) \; .$$

*Moreover, the time complexities of the extractor*  $\mathcal{E}$  *and adversaries*  $\mathcal{F}_1, \mathcal{F}_2, \mathcal{F}_3$  *are all*  $O(q \cdot n)$ .

We can show that the bound in Theorem 7 is tight by constructing a cheating prover like we did in Theorem 5. Using Theorem 2, we get a corollary about fs-ext-1 security of  $FS^{RO}[SnACSPf]$ .

**Corollary 3.** Let  $\mathbb{G} = \{\mathbb{G}_{\lambda}\}_{{\lambda} \in \mathbb{N}^+}$  be a family of groups with order  $p = p(\lambda)$ . Let  $\mathbb{G}_T = \{\mathbb{G}_{T,\lambda}\}_{{\lambda} \in \mathbb{N}^+}$  be a family of groups such that there exists a bilinear map  $e : \mathbb{G} \times \mathbb{G} \to \mathbb{G}_T$ . Let  $\mathsf{SnACSPf} = \mathsf{SnACSPf} [\mathbb{G}, \mathbb{G}_T, e]$

be the interactive argument as described in Figure 16, for the relation R in (11). Let  $\mathsf{FS^{RO}}[\mathsf{SnACSPf}]$  be the non-interactive argument obtained by applying the Fiat-Shamir transform to  $\mathsf{SnACSPf}$  using a random oracle. We can construct an extractor  $\mathcal E$  such that for any non-uniform algebraic prover  $\mathcal P_{\mathsf{alg}}$  making at most  $q=q(\lambda)$  queries to the random oracle there exist non-uniform adversaries  $\mathcal F_1, \mathcal F_2, \mathcal F_3$  with the property that for all  $\lambda \in \mathbb N^+$ ,

$$\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{FS}^{\mathbf{RO}}[\mathsf{SnACSPf}],R}^{\mathsf{fs\text{-}ext-1}}(\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}},\mathcal{E},\lambda) \leqslant \frac{18nq+q+1}{p-1} + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathbb{G}}^{4n\text{-}\mathsf{dI}}(\mathcal{F}_1,\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathbb{G}}^{\mathsf{dI}}(\mathcal{F}_2,\lambda) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathbb{G}}^{\mathsf{dI}}(\mathcal{F}_3,\lambda) \;.$$

Moreover, the time complexities of the extractor  $\mathcal{E}$  and adversaries  $\mathcal{F}_1, \mathcal{F}_2, \mathcal{F}_3$  are all  $O(q \cdot n)$ .

Additionally, using techniques similar to those in the proof of Theorem 7, we can prove a similar bound for fs-ext-2 security of FS<sup>RO</sup>[SnACSPf].

<span id="page-46-0"></span>Fig. 21. Well-formedness argument in Sonic

*Proof.* (Theorem 7) We shall invoke Theorem 1 by defining BadCh and e and showing that  $\varepsilon \leqslant \frac{18n}{p-1}$  and there exists adversaries  $\mathcal{F}_1, \mathcal{F}_2, \mathcal{F}_3$  such that

$$p_{\mathsf{fail}}(\mathsf{SnACSPf}, \mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}, \mathsf{e}, R, \lambda) \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathbb{G}}^{4n-\mathsf{dl}}(\mathcal{F}_1) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathbb{G}}^{\mathsf{dl}}(\mathcal{F}_2) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathbb{G}}^{\mathsf{dl}}(\mathcal{F}_3)$$
.

DEFINING BadCh AND UPPER BOUNDING  $\varepsilon$ . To start off, we shall define BadCh( $\tau'$ ) for all partial extended transcripts  $\tau'$ . Let Ch be the set from which the challenge that comes right after  $\tau'$  is sampled. We define a helper function CheckBad that takes as input a partial extended transcripts  $[\tau']$  and a challenge  $c \in \mathbb{C}$  had returns true if and only if  $c \in \mathsf{BadCh}(\tau')$ . Since SnACSPf has two challenges, there are two definitions of CheckBad in Figure 22. We again use the predicate SZ here like before. Next, we need to compute an upper bound  $\varepsilon$  on the size of  $|\mathsf{BadCh}(\tau')|/|\mathsf{Ch}|$ . In other words, we need to compute an upper bound on the fraction of c's in Ch that  $\mathsf{CheckBad}(\tau',c)$  will return true for all the definitions of  $\mathsf{CheckBad}$ .

The function  $\operatorname{CheckBad}(\tau',y)$  returns true if  $\operatorname{SZ}(f(Y),y)$  is true. We shall use the Schwartz-Zippel lemma to fraction bound the number of y's that  $\operatorname{SZ}(f(Y),y)$  is true for  $y\in\mathbb{Z}_p^*$ . The polynomial f(Y) is a polynomial of degree at most 2n+Q (the maximum positive degree is n+Q while the maximum negative degree is -n). Since  $Q\leqslant 2n$ , the degree of f(Y) is at most 4n. So, for at most 4n values of  $y\in\mathbb{Z}_p^*$ ,  $\operatorname{SZ}(f(Y),y)$  is true. So the  $\operatorname{CheckBad}(\tau',y)$  returns true for at most 4n/(p-1) fraction of y's.

The function  $\operatorname{CheckBad}(\tau',z)$  returns true if  $\operatorname{SZ}(f(Z),z)$  is true. The polynomial f(Z) is a polynomial of degree at most 18n (the maximum positive degree is d<4n while the maximum negative degree is 2n-4d>-16d). So, the fraction of z's in  $\mathbb{Z}_p^*$  for which  $\operatorname{SZ}(f(Z),z)$  is true is at most 18n/(p-1). So the fraction of z's in  $\mathbb{Z}_p^*$  for which  $\operatorname{CheckBad}(\tau',z)$  returns true is at most 18n/(p-1).

Similarly we can argue that for  $j=1,\ldots,M$ , CheckBad $(\tau',z_j)$  returns true with probability at most (10n+1)/(p-1), CheckBad $(\tau',y_j)$  returns true with probability at most (2n+2)/(p-1), CheckBad $(\tau',(\beta_j,\gamma_j))$  returns true with probability at most n/(p-1), CheckBad $(\tau',\delta_j)$  returns true with probability at most 8n/(p-1).

Therefore CheckBad $(\tau',c)$  will return true for any partial transcript  $\tau'$  for a no more than 18n/(p-1) values of c, i.e., in the context of the Master Theorem  $\varepsilon \leqslant \frac{18n}{p-1}$ .

DEFINING e. Next, we define the function e for SnACSPf in Figure 23. It gets as input an extended accepting transcript  $[\tau]$  with the representation of the input removed. Without loss of generality we assume that the representations of all the messages of the prover in the transcript that are from  $\mathbb{G}$  are in terms of the elements of  $\mathbb{G}$  in srs. The function e computes  $(\mathbf{a}_L^*, \mathbf{a}_R^*, \mathbf{a}_O^*)$  and outputs them. It follows from the description of e that it runs in time O(n). Note that SnACSPf.V runs in time O(n). Therefore, using Theorem 1, the time complexity of  $\mathcal{E}$  is  $O(q \cdot n)$ .

PROVING AN UPPER BOUND ON  $p_{\mathsf{fail}}(\mathsf{SnACSPf}, \mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}, \mathsf{e}, R, \lambda)$ . To that end, we construct the following three adversaries  $\mathcal{F}_1, \mathcal{F}_2, \mathcal{F}_3$ .

$$\begin{split} & \frac{\operatorname{Procedure CheckBad}([\tau'],z):}{f(Z) \leftarrow \left(\sum\limits_{i=-d}^{d} Z^{i}t_{g^{\alpha x^{i}}}\right) - \left(\sum\limits_{i=n-2d}^{n} Z^{i}r_{g^{\alpha x^{i-n+d}}}\right) \left(\sum\limits_{i=n-2d}^{n} (yZ)^{i}r_{g^{\alpha x^{i-n+d}}} - s(Z,y)\right) + k(y) \\ & \operatorname{Returm SZ}(f(Z),z) \end{split}$$

$$& \operatorname{Procedure CheckBad}([\tau'],y): \\ & \operatorname{For} i = 1, \dots, n \text{ do} \\ & a_{i}^{*} \leftarrow r_{g^{\alpha x^{d-n+i}}}; b_{i}^{*} \leftarrow r_{g^{\alpha x^{d-n-i}}}; c_{i}^{*} \leftarrow r_{g^{\alpha x^{d-2n-i}}} \\ & a_{i}^{*} \leftarrow (a_{1}^{*}, \dots, a_{n}^{*}); a_{K}^{*} \leftarrow (b_{1}^{*}, \dots, b_{N}^{*}); a_{K}^{*} \leftarrow (c_{1}^{*}, \dots, c_{n}^{*}) \\ & f(Y) \leftarrow r_{g^{\alpha x^{i-n}}} + (a_{2}^{*}, \dots, a_{N}^{*}); <span id="page-47-0"></span>Fig. 22. The function CheckBad function for the SnACSPf.

Return  $SZ(f(\Delta), \delta_j)$ 

# $\begin{aligned} & \underbrace{ \text{Procedure e}([\tau]):} \\ & //[\tau] = \left( \text{bp, srs}, n, d, s(X, Y), k(Y), \{\psi_j(X, Y), \sigma_j\}_{j=1}^M; [R], y, [T], z, (a, [W_a], b, [W_b], [W_t], s), \{([S_i, S_i']), (\delta_i, \beta_i, \gamma_i), (S_i, [W_i], v_i, [W_i'], [Q_i']), ([A_i, C_i, C_{i,w}, U_{i,w}, V_{i,w}], a_{i,n+1}), y_i, T_i, z_i, (a_i, [W_{i,a}], b_i, [W_{i,b}], k_i, [W_{i,k}], [W_{i,t}]) \}_{i=1}^M \right) \\ & a_i^* \leftarrow r_{g^{\alpha x^{d-n+i}}}; b_i^* \leftarrow r_{g^{\alpha x^{d-n-i}}}; c_i^* \leftarrow r_{g^{\alpha x^{d-2n-i}}} \\ & a_L^* \leftarrow (a_1^*, \dots, a_n^*); \mathbf{a}_R^* \leftarrow (b_1^*, \dots, b_n^*); \mathbf{a}_O^* \leftarrow (c_1^*, \dots, c_n^*) \\ & \text{Return } (\mathbf{a}_L^*, \mathbf{a}_R^*, \mathbf{a}_O^*) \end{aligned}$

Note that  $(n, d, \mathsf{bp}, \mathsf{srs})$  is a valid output of SnACSPf.Setup. Adversary  $\mathcal{F}_1$  runs  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  on public parameters  $(n, d, \mathsf{bp}, \mathsf{srs})$  and simulates the game  $\mathsf{SRS}_{\mathsf{SnACSPf}}$  to it. If  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  manages to produce an accepting transcript  $\tau$ ,  $\mathcal{F}_1$  calls a helper function  $\mathsf{h}_1$  on input  $[\tau]$ ,  $\alpha$ ,  $\beta$ ,  $g^x$  and outputs whatever  $\mathsf{h}_1$  outputs. The function  $\mathsf{h}_1$  is defined in Figure 24. The subroutines used in  $\mathsf{h}_1$  are defined in Figures 27 to 29.

2. Adversary  $\mathcal{F}_2$  is an adversary against DLOG in the group  $\mathbb{G}$  that runs  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$ . It has inputs (g,V). It fixes a positive integer n such that 4n>d>3n. It samples  $\alpha,x\in\mathbb{Z}_p$ , and sets  $\mathsf{bp}=(p,\mathbb{G},\mathbb{G}_T,e,g,V)$  and

$$\mathrm{srs} = \{g, \{g^{x^i}\}_{i=-d}^d, \{V^{x^i}\}_{i=-d}^d, \{V^{x^{i}}^\alpha\}_{i=-d}^d, \{g^{x^{i}}^\alpha\}_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d, e(g, V^\alpha)\}\;.$$

Note that  $(n,d,\mathsf{bp},\mathsf{srs})$  is a valid output of SnACSPf.Setup. Adversary  $\mathcal{F}_2$  runs  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  on public parameters  $(n,d,\mathsf{bp},\mathsf{srs})$  and simulates the game  $\mathsf{SRS}_{\mathsf{SnACSPf}}$  to it. If  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  manages to produce an accepting transcript  $\tau$ ,  $\mathcal{F}_2$  calls a helper function  $\mathsf{h}_2$  on input  $[\tau]$ ,  $x,\alpha,V$  and outputs whatever  $\mathsf{h}_2$  outputs. The function  $\mathsf{h}_2$  is defined in Figure 25. The subroutines used in  $\mathsf{h}_2$  are defined in Figures 27 to 29.

```
           \beta^* \leftarrow \mathsf{ComHelper}_2(X, x, \alpha, [C_i], [\tilde{W}_{i,c}], c_i, z^{-1}, d); \text{ If } \beta^* \neq \bot \text{ then return } \beta^*
          \begin{array}{l} \beta^{*} \leftarrow \mathsf{ComHelper}_{2}(X, x, \alpha, [C_{i}], [W_{i,k}], k_{i}, y, d); \mathsf{If} \ \beta^{*} \neq \bot \ \mathsf{then} \ \mathsf{return} \ \beta^{*} \\ \beta^{*} \leftarrow \mathsf{ComHelper}_{2}(X, x, \alpha, [T_{i}], [W_{i,t}], t_{i}, z, d); \mathsf{If} \ \beta^{*} \neq \bot \ \mathsf{then} \ \mathsf{return} \ \beta^{*} \end{array}
           \beta^* \leftarrow \mathsf{EqHelper}_2(X, x, \alpha, [U_i], [V_i], [A_i], a_{i,n+1}, n); \mathsf{If} \ \beta^* \neq \bot \mathsf{then} \ \mathsf{return} \ \beta^*
           \beta^* \leftarrow \mathsf{WfHelper}_2(X, x, \alpha, [C], [C_{i,w,1}, C_{i,w,2}], 2n+1); \mathsf{If } \beta^* \neq \bot \mathsf{then return } \beta^*
           \beta^* \leftarrow \mathsf{WfHelper}_2(X, x, \alpha, [U], [U_{i,w,1}, U_{i,w,2}], n); \mathsf{If} \ \beta^* \neq \bot \mathsf{then} \ \mathsf{return} \ \beta^*
           \beta^* \leftarrow \mathsf{WfHelper}_2(X, x, \alpha, [V], [V_{i,w,1}, V_{i,w,2}], n); \mathsf{If} \ \beta^* \neq \bot \mathsf{then} \ \mathsf{return} \ \beta^*
Return \
```

<span id="page-49-0"></span>Fig. 25. The function h<sub>2</sub> for SnACSPf.

3. Adversary  $\mathcal{F}_3$  is an adversary against DLOG in the group  $\mathbb{G}$  that runs  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$ . It has inputs (g,V). It fixes a positive integer n such that 4n>d>3n. It samples  $\beta,x\in\mathbb{Z}_p$ , and sets  $\mathsf{bp}=(p,\mathbb{G},\mathbb{G}_T,e,g,g^\beta)$  and

$$\mathrm{srs} = \{g, \{g^{x^i}\}_{i=-d}^d, \{g^{\beta x^i}\}_{i=-d}^d, \{{V^{x^i}}^\beta\}_{i=-d}^d, \{{V^{x^i}}^\beta\}_{i=-d}^d, e(g, V^\beta)\} \;.$$

Note that  $(n,d,\mathsf{bp},\mathsf{srs})$  is a valid output of SnACSPf.Setup. Adversary  $\mathcal{F}_3$  runs  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  on public parameters  $(n,d,\mathsf{bp},\mathsf{srs})$  and simulates the game  $\mathsf{SRS}_{\mathsf{SnACSPf}}$  to it. If  $\mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}$  manages to produce an accepting transcript  $\tau$ ,  $\mathcal{F}_3$  calls a helper function  $\mathsf{h}_3$  on input  $[\tau]$ ,  $x,\beta,V$  and outputs whatever  $\mathsf{h}_3$  outputs. The function  $\mathsf{h}_3$  is defined in Figure 26. The subroutines used in  $\mathsf{h}_3$  are defined in Figures 27 to 29.

Note that the definitions of the helper functions are modular, i.e.,  $h_i$  use the subroutines  $PC_i$ ,  $EqHelper_i$ ,  $WfHelper_i$  for i=1,2,3. The subroutine  $PC_i$  produces a solution to the relevant hard problem if the prover manages to break the binding of any of the commitment. Similarly the subroutine  $WfHelper_i$  produces a solution to the relevant hard problem if the prover manages to pass the well-formedness verification for a commitment that is not well-formed.

We now make the following observations about adversaries  $\mathcal{F}_1, \mathcal{F}_2, \mathcal{F}_3$ 

- Adversary  $\mathcal{F}_1$  succeeds if  $\mathsf{h}_1([\tau], \alpha, \beta)$  computes  $x^*$  such that  $(g^{x^*} = g^x)$ . From the code of  $\mathsf{h}_1$  it is easy to see that that whenever  $\mathsf{h}_1$  returns a non- $\bot$  value  $x^*$ , it satisfies  $(g^{x^*} = g^x)$ , i.e., adversary  $\mathcal{F}_1$  succeeds. Also, it follows from the description of  $\mathsf{h}_1$  that it runs in time at O(n)

(since M = O(1)). The running time of  $\mathcal{F}_1$  consists of the time required to answers q queries, run SnACSPf.V in at most q paths in the execution tree and the time required to run  $h_1$ . Hence its time complexity is O(qn).

- Adversary  $\mathcal{F}_2$  succeeds if  $\mathsf{h}_2([\tau], x, \alpha)$  computes  $\beta^*$  such that  $g^{\beta^*} = V$ . From the code of  $\mathsf{h}_2$  it is easy to see that that whenever  $\mathsf{h}_2$  returns a non- $\bot$  value  $\beta^*$ , it satisfies  $(g^{\beta^*} = h)$ , i.e., adversary  $\mathcal{F}_2$  succeeds. Also, it follows from the description of  $\mathsf{h}_2$  that it runs in time O(n) (since M = O(1)). The running time of  $\mathcal{F}_2$  consists of the time required to answers q queries, run SnACSPf.V in at most q paths in the execution tree and the time required to run  $\mathsf{h}_2$ . Hence its time complexity is O(qn).
- Adversary  $\mathcal{F}_3$  succeeds if  $h_3(\tau, x, \beta)$  computes  $\alpha^*$  such that  $g^{\alpha^*} = V$ . From the code of  $h_3$  it is easy to see that that whenever  $h_3$  returns a non- $\bot$  value  $\alpha^*$ , it satisfies  $(g^{\alpha^*} = g^x)$ , i.e., adversary  $\mathcal{F}_3$  succeeds. Also, it follows from the description of  $h_3$  that it runs in time O(n) (since M = O(1)). The running time of  $\mathcal{F}_3$  consists of the time required to answers q queries, run SnACSPf.V in at most q paths in the execution tree and the time required to run  $h_3$ . Hence its time complexity is O(qn).

<span id="page-50-1"></span>We shall prove the following lemma showing that if  $\tau$  is an accepting transcript such that  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}^{\mathsf{SnACSPf}}$  and  $\mathsf{h}_1([\tau],\alpha,\beta)$ ,  $\mathsf{h}_2([\tau],x,\alpha)$ ,  $\mathsf{h}_3(\tau,x,\beta)$  all return  $\bot$ , then  $\mathsf{e}([\tau])$  returns a valid witness.

$$\mathbf{Procedure}\;\mathsf{ComHelper}_{1}(X,\left[C\right],\left[W\right],v,z,n)$$

$$f(X) \leftarrow (X - z) \left( \sum_{i = -d}^{d} X^{i} w_{g^{x^{i}}} \right) + v - X^{-d + n} \left( \sum_{\substack{i = -d \\ i \neq 0}}^{d} X^{i} c_{g^{\alpha x^{i}}} \right)$$

If  $f(X) \neq 0$  then

Solve for  $x^*$  such that  $f(x^*) = 0$ 

If  $X = g^{x^*}$  then return  $x^*$

If  $f(B) \neq 0$  then

Solve for  $\beta^*$  such that  $f(\beta^*) = 0$ 

If  $X = g^{\beta^*}$  then return  $\beta^*$ 

 $\begin{array}{l} \operatorname{Return} \perp \\ \operatorname{\mathbf{Procedure}} \operatorname{\mathsf{ComHelper}}_3(X,x,\left[C\right],\left[W\right],v,z,n) \end{array}$ 

$$\overline{f(\mathbf{A}) \leftarrow \mathbf{A}(x-z) \left(\sum_{i=-d}^{d} x^i w_{g^{x^i}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^{d} \mathbf{A} x^i w_{g^{\alpha x^i}}\right) + \mathbf{A} v - x^{-d+n} \left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^{d} x^i c_{g^{x^i}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^{d} \mathbf{A} x^i c_{g^{\alpha x^i}}\right)$$

<span id="page-51-0"></span>**Fig. 27.** Subroutines for  $h_1, h_2, h_3$ .

**Lemma 11.** Let  $n, d \in \mathbb{N}$  such that d > 3n. Let  $x, \alpha, \beta \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ , bp =  $(p, \mathbb{G}, \mathbb{G}_T, e, g, h)$ . Let srs =  $\{g, \{g^{x^i}\}_{i=-d}^d, \{g^{\beta x^i}\}_{i=-d}^d, \{g^{\alpha\beta x^i}\}_{i=-d}^d, \{g^{\alpha x^i}\}_{i=-d}^d, e(g, h^{\alpha})\}.$  Let

$$\begin{split} \tau &= \left(\mathsf{bp},\mathsf{srs},n,d,s(X,Y),k(Y),\{\psi_j(X,Y),\sigma_j\}_{j=1}^M;[R]\,,y,[T]\,,z,(a,[W_a]\,,b,[W_b]\,,\\ &[W_t]\,,s),\{(\left[S_i,S_i'\right]),(\delta_i,\beta_i,\gamma_i),(s_i,[W_i]\,,v_i,\left[W_i'\right],\left[Q_i'\right]),(\left[A_i,C_i,C_{i,w},U_{i,w},V_{i,w}\right],\\ &a_{i,n+1}),y_i,T_i,z_i,(a_i,[W_{i,a}]\,,b_i,[W_{i,b}]\,,k_i,[W_{i,k}]\,,\left[W_{i,t}\right])\}_{i=1}^M \end{split}$$

be an accepting transcript of SnACSPf such that  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}^{\mathsf{SnACSPf}}$ . If  $\mathsf{h}_1([\tau], \alpha, \beta, g^x)$ ,  $\mathsf{h}_2([\tau], x, \alpha, V)$  and  $h_3([\tau], x, \beta, V)$  return  $\bot$ , then  $e([\tau])$  returns  $(\mathbf{a}_L^*, \mathbf{a}_R^*, \mathbf{a}_O^*)$  such that

$$\mathbf{a}_L^* \circ \mathbf{a}_R^* = \mathbf{a}_O^*$$
 and  $\mathbf{a}_L^* \cdot \mathbf{W}_L + \mathbf{a}_R^* \cdot \mathbf{W}_R + \mathbf{a}_O^* \cdot \mathbf{W}_O = \mathbf{c}$ .

Taking the contrapositive, we get that if  $\tau$  is an accepting transcript such that  $\tau \notin \mathcal{T}_{BadCh}^{SnACSPf}$  and  $e([\tau])$  fails to return a valid witness, then one of  $h_1([\tau], \alpha, \beta, g^x)$ ,  $h_2([\tau], x, \alpha, V)$ ,  $h_3(\tau, x, \beta, V)$  returns a non- $\perp$  value, i.e., one of adversaries  $\mathcal{F}_1, \mathcal{F}_2, \mathcal{F}_3$  succeed. Therefore

$$p_{\mathsf{fail}}(\mathsf{SnACSPf}, \mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{alg}}, \mathsf{e}, R, \lambda) \leqslant \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathbb{G}}^{4n\text{-dl}}(\mathcal{F}_1) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathbb{G}}^{\mathsf{dl}}(\mathcal{F}_2) + \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathbb{G}}^{\mathsf{dl}}(\mathcal{F}_3) \; .$$

We shall next prove Lemma 11.

$$\begin{split} & \underbrace{Procedure \ \mathsf{EqHelper}_1(X,[U],[V],[A],a_{n+1},n)}_{f(X) \leftarrow \left(\sum\limits_{i=-d}^d X^i u_{g\alpha^{x^i}} + X^{i+n+1} v_{g\alpha^{x^i}}\right) + a_{n+1} X^{n+1} - \left(\sum\limits_{i=-d}^d X^i a_{g\alpha^{x^i}}\right)}_{i\neq 0} \\ & \text{If } f(X) \neq 0 \text{ then } \\ & \text{Solve for } x^* \text{ such that } f(x^*) = 0 \\ & \text{If } X = g^{x^*} \text{ then return } x^* \\ & \text{Return} \bot \\ & \underbrace{Procedure}_{i=-d} \text{EqHelper}_2(X,x,\alpha,[U],[V],[A],a_{n+1},n) : \\ & f(B) \leftarrow \left(\sum\limits_{i=-d}^d x^i u_{gx^i} + x^{i+n+1} v_{gx^i} + \sum\limits_{i=-d}^d \alpha x^i u_{g\alpha^{x^i}} + x^{i+n+1} v_{g\alpha^{x^i}}\right) \\ & + B\left(\sum\limits_{i=-d}^d x^i u_{hx^i} + \alpha x^i u_{h\alpha^{x^i}} + x^{i+n+1} v_{hx^i} + \alpha x^{i+n+1} v_{h\alpha^{x^i}} - \sum\limits_{i=-d}^d x^i a_{hx^i} + \alpha x^i a_{h\alpha^{x^i}}\right) + \alpha a_{n+1} x^{n+1} \\ & - \left(\sum\limits_{i=-d}^d x^i a_{gx^i} + \sum\limits_{i=-d}^d \alpha x^i a_{g\alpha^{x^i}}\right) \\ & \text{If } f(B) \neq 0 \text{ then } \\ & \text{Solve for } \beta^* \text{ such that } f(\beta^*) = 0 \\ & \text{If } X = g^{\beta^*} \text{ then return } \beta^* \\ & \text{Return } \bot \\ & \underbrace{Procedure}_{i=-d} \text{EqHelper}_3(X,x,[U],[V],[A],a_{n+1,n}) \\ & f(A) \leftarrow \left(\sum\limits_{i=-d}^d x^i u_{gx^i} + x^{i+n+1} v_{gx^i} + \sum\limits_{i=-d}^d A x^i u_{g\alpha^{x^i}} + x^{i+n+1} v_{g\alpha^{x^i}}\right) + A a_{n+1} x^{n+1} - \left(\sum\limits_{i=-d}^d x^i a_{gx^i} + \sum\limits_{i=-d}^d A x^i a_{g\alpha^{x^i}}\right) \\ & \text{If } f(A) \neq 0 \text{ then } \\ & \text{Solve for } \alpha^* \text{ such that } f(\alpha^*) = 0 \\ & \text{If } X = g^{\alpha^*} \text{ then return } \alpha^* \\ & \text{Return } \bot \end{aligned}$$

**Fig. 28.** Subroutines for h1, h2, h3.

*Proof (Lemma [11\)](#page-50-1).* Since τ is an accepting transcript the following equality holds.

$$e(W_a, h^{\alpha x})e(g^aW_a^z, h^{\alpha}) = e(R, h^{x^{-d+n}}).$$

We can express W<sup>a</sup> in terms of its representations, let h g <sup>β</sup> and re-write the first equality as

$$e(g,h)^f = 1 \; ,$$

where

$$\begin{split} f = &\alpha(x-z)\left(\sum_{i=-d}^{d}x^{i}w_{ag^{x^{i}}} + \beta x^{i}w_{ah^{x^{i}}} + \alpha\beta x^{i}w_{ah^{\alpha x^{i}}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^{d}\alpha x^{i}w_{ag^{\alpha x^{i}}}\right) + \alpha a^{i}w_{ag^{x^{i}}} + \alpha\beta x^{i}r_{h^{x^{i}}} + \alpha\beta x^{i}r_{h^{\alpha x^{i}}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^{d}\alpha x^{i}r_{g^{\alpha x^{i}}}\right). \end{split}$$

#### **Procedure** WfHelper<sup>1</sup> pX,rAs,rL, Rs, nq : f1pXq Ð x d °d id X i l gxi °d id i0 AX i agαxi If f1pXq 0 then Solve for x such that f1px q 0 If X g x then return x Return K f2pXq Ð X nd °d id X i r gxi °d id i0 X i agαxi If f2pXq 0 then Solve for x such that f2px q 0 If X g x then return x

Return K

**Procedure** WfHelper<sup>2</sup> pX, x, α,rAs,rL, Rs, nq :

$$\begin{split} f_1(\mathbf{B}) \leftarrow \mathbf{B} \left( \alpha x^d \left( \sum_{i=-d}^d x^i l_{h^{x^i}} + \alpha x^i l_{h^{\alpha x^i}} \right) - \left( \sum_{i=-d}^d x^i a_{h^{x^i}} + \alpha x^i a_{h^{\alpha x^i}} \right) \right) + \alpha x^d \left( \sum_{i=-d}^d x^i l_{g^{x^i}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d \\ i \neq 0}}^d \alpha x^i l_{g^{\alpha x^i}} \right) \\ - \left( \sum_{i=-d}^d x^i a_{g^{x^i}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d \\ i \neq 0}}^d \alpha x^i a_{g^{\alpha x^i}} \right) \end{split}$$

If f1pBq 0 then

Solve for β such that f1pβ q 0

If X g β then return β 

$$\begin{split} f_2(\mathbf{B}) \leftarrow \mathbf{B} \left( \alpha x^{n-d} \left( \sum_{i=-d}^d x^i r_{h^{x^i}} + \alpha x^i r_{h^{\alpha x^i}} \right) - \left( \sum_{i=-d}^d x^i a_{h^{x^i}} + \alpha x^i a_{h^{\alpha x^i}} \right) \right) + \alpha x^{n-d} \left( \sum_{i=-d}^d x^i r_{g^{x^i}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d \alpha x^i r_{g^{\alpha x^i}} \right) \\ - \left( \sum_{i=-d}^d x^i a_{g^{x^i}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d \alpha x^i a_{g^{\alpha x^i}} \right) \end{split}$$

If f2pBq 0 then

Solve for β such that f2pβ q 0

If X g β then return β 

Return K

**Procedure** WfHelper<sup>3</sup> pX, x,rAs,rL, Rs, nq :

$$f_1(\mathbf{A}) \leftarrow \mathbf{A} x^d \left( \sum_{i=-d}^d x^i l_{g^{x^i}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d \mathbf{A} x^i l_{g^{\alpha x^i}} \right) - \left( \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d x^i a_{g^{x^i}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d \mathbf{A} x^i a_{g^{\alpha x^i}} \right)$$

If f1pAq 0 then

Solve for α such that f1pα q 0

If X g α then return α 

$$f_2(\mathbf{A}) \leftarrow \mathbf{A} x^{n-d} \left( \sum_{i=-d}^d x^i r_{gx^i} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d \mathbf{A} x^i r_{g^{\alpha x^i}} \right) - \left( \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d x^i a_{g^{x^i}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d \mathbf{A} x^i a_{g^{\alpha x^i}} \right)$$

If f2pAq 0 then

Solve for α such that f2pα q 0

If X g α then return α 

Return K

<span id="page-53-0"></span>**Fig. 29.** Subroutines for h1, h2, h3.

<span id="page-54-0"></span>We therefore have

$$\alpha(x-z) \left( \sum_{i=-d}^{d} x^{i} w_{ag^{x^{i}}} + \beta x^{i} w_{ah^{x^{i}}} + \alpha \beta x^{i} w_{ah^{\alpha x^{i}}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^{d} \alpha x^{i} w_{ag^{\alpha x^{i}}} \right) + \alpha a - x^{-d+n} \left( \sum_{i=-d}^{d} x^{i} r_{g^{x^{i}}} + \beta x^{i} r_{h^{x^{i}}} + \alpha \beta x^{i} r_{h^{\alpha x^{i}}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^{d} \alpha x^{i} r_{g^{\alpha x^{i}}} \right) = 0.$$
(27)

Therefore β is a root fpBq 0 in ComHelper<sup>2</sup> pX, x, α,rRs,rWas, a, z, nq invoked by h2. Since h2prτ s, x, α, V q returned K we have that fpBq must be the zero polynomial, i.e.,

$$\alpha(x-z)\left(\sum_{i=-d}^d x^i w_{ah^{x^i}} + \alpha x^i w_{ah^{\alpha x^i}}\right) - x^{-d+n}\left(\sum_{i=-d}^d x^i r_{h^{x^i}} + \alpha x^i r_{h^{\alpha x^i}}\right) = 0 \ .$$

Plugging this into [\(27\)](#page-54-0) we get that

$$\begin{split} &\alpha(x-z)\left(\sum_{i=-d}^d x^iw_{ag^{x^i}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d \alpha x^iw_{ag^{\alpha x^i}}\right) + \alpha a\\ &-x^{-d+n}\left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d x^ir_{g^{x^i}} + \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d \alpha x^ir_{g^{\alpha x^i}}\right) = 0\;. \end{split}$$

Therefore α is a root fpAq 0 in ComHelper<sup>3</sup> pX, x,rRs,rWas, a, z, nqinvoked by h3. Since h3prτ s, x, β, V q returned K it means that fpAq is the zero polynomial. In particular its A term is 0 i.e.

$$(x-z) \left( \sum_{i=-d}^{d} x^{i} w_{ag^{x^{i}}} \right) + a - x^{-d+n} \left( \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^{d} x^{i} r_{g^{\alpha x^{i}}} \right) = 0.$$

Therefore x is a root fpXq 0 in ComHelper<sup>1</sup> pX,rRs,rWas, a, z, nq invoked by h1. Now, since h1prτ s, x, β, g<sup>x</sup> q returned K we have that f1pXq is the zero polynomial, i.e.,

$$(X-z)\left(\sum_{i=-d}^d X^i w_{ag^{x^i}}\right) + a - X^{-d+n}\left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d X^i r_{g^{\alpha x^i}}\right).$$

is the zero polynomial. The above polynomial is an zero for any value of X. So, plugging in X z we get

$$a - z^{-d+n} \left( \sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d z^i r_{g^{\alpha x^i}} \right) = 0.$$

So,

$$a = \left(\sum_{\substack{i=n-2d\\i\neq n-d}}^{n} z^{i} r_{g^{\alpha x^{i-n+d}}}\right).$$

Similarly, since  $\tau$  is an accepting transcript, the equalities

$$e(W_b, h^{\alpha x})e(g^bW_b^{yz}, h^{\alpha}) = e(R, h^{x^{-d+n}}), e(W_t, h^{\alpha x})e(g^tW_t^z, h^{\alpha}) = e(T, h)$$

hold. Using arguments similar to the ones we used above, we can show that

$$b = \left(\sum_{\substack{i=n-2d\\i\neq n-d}}^{n} (yz)^{i} r_{g^{\alpha x^{i-n+d}}}\right), \ t = \left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^{d} z^{i} t_{g^{\alpha x^{i}}}\right).$$

Next we can show that for the opening of commitments  $T_j$ ,  $C_j$ ,  $A_j$  (similar to how we derived the value for a above) for j = 1, ..., M

$$t_j = \left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d z_j^i t_{jg^{\alpha x^i}}\right), k_j = \left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d y_j^i c_{jg^{\alpha x^i}}\right), c_j = \left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d z_j^{-i} c_{jg^{\alpha x^i}}\right), a_j = \left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d (y_j z_j)^i a_{jg^{\alpha x^i}}\right).$$

Also using that for j = 1, ..., M,

$$\begin{split} & \mathsf{WfHelper}_1(g^x, [C] \,, [C_{j,w,1}, C_{j,w,2}] \,, 2n+1) = \bot \,, \\ & \mathsf{WfHelper}_2(V, x, \alpha, [C] \,, [C_{j,w,1}, C_{j,w,2}] \,, 2n+1) = \bot \,, \\ & \mathsf{WfHelper}_3(X, x, [C] \,, [C_{j,w,1}, C_{j,w,2}] \,, 2n+1) = \bot \,, \end{split}$$

we can show that  $c_{jg^{\alpha x^i}}=0$  for i<=0 and for i>2n+1 and  $c_{jg^{x^i}}=0$ ,  $c_{jh^{\alpha x^i}}=0$ ,  $c_{jh^{x^i}}=0$  for all i. Similarly, we can show that  $u_{jg^{\alpha x^i}}=0$  for i<=0 and for i>n and  $u_{jg^{x^i}}=0$ ,  $u_{jh^{\alpha x^i}}=0$ ,  $u_{jh^{x^i}}=0$  for all i and  $v_{jg^{\alpha x^i}}=0$  for i<=0 and for i>n and  $v_{jg^{x^i}}=0$ ,  $v_{jh^{\alpha x^i}}=0$ , for all i.

Hence  $c_j = \left(\sum_{i=1}^{2n+1} z_j^{-i} c_{jg^{\alpha x^i}}\right)$ . We also have that  $t_j = (ya_j + z_j^{n+2} + z_j^{n+1} y_j - z_j^{2n+2} y_j)(c_j + 1)z_j^{-1} - y_j k_j - 1$ . Therefore, for  $j = 1, \dots, M$ 

$$\begin{pmatrix} \sum_{i=-d}^{d} z_{j}^{i} t_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} \end{pmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix} y_{j} \begin{pmatrix} \sum_{i=-d}^{d} (y_{j}z_{j})^{i} a_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} \\ \sum_{i=1}^{d} z_{j}^{n+2} + z_{j}^{n+1} y - z_{j}^{2n+2} y_{j} \end{pmatrix} \cdot \begin{pmatrix} \sum_{i=1}^{2n+1} z_{j}^{-i} c_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} + 1 \end{pmatrix} z_{j}^{-1} - \begin{pmatrix} \sum_{i=1}^{2n+1} y_{j}^{i} c_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} \\ \sum_{i=1}^{n+1} z_{j}^{-i} c_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} + 1 \end{pmatrix} z_{j}^{-1} - \begin{pmatrix} \sum_{i=1}^{2n+1} y_{j}^{i} c_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} \\ \sum_{i=1}^{n+1} z_{j}^{-i} c_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} + 1 \end{pmatrix} z_{j}^{-1} - \begin{pmatrix} \sum_{i=1}^{2n+1} y_{i}^{i} c_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} \\ \sum_{i=1}^{n+1} z_{j}^{-i} c_{ig^{\alpha x^{i}}} \end{pmatrix} y_{j} - 1 .$$

Since  $\tau|_{z_j} \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}^{\mathsf{SnACSPf}}$ , we have that  $z_j \notin \mathsf{BadCh}(\tau|_{z_j})$ . Therefore,  $\mathsf{SZ}(f(Z), z_j)$  is false where f is as defined in  $\mathsf{CheckBad}(\tau', z_j)$ . Since we have here that  $f(z_j) = 0$ , the polynomial f(Z) is the zero polynomial. In particular, its constant term is zero, i.e.,

$$\sum_{i=1}^{2n+1} y_j^{i+1} \left( a_{jg^{\alpha x^i}} c_{jg^{\alpha x^{i-1}}} - c_{jg^{\alpha x^{i-1}}} \right) + \left( c_{jg^{\alpha x^{n+1}}} - 1 \right) + y_j \left( c_{jg^{\alpha x^n}} - c_{jg^{\alpha x^{2n+1}}} \right) = 0.$$

Since  $\tau|_{y_j} \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}^{\mathsf{SnACSPf}}$ , we have that  $y_j \notin \mathsf{BadCh}(\tau|_{y_j})$ . Therefore,  $\mathsf{SZ}(f(Y), y_j)$  is false where f is as defined in  $\mathsf{CheckBad}(\tau', y_j)$ . Since we have here that  $f(y_j) = 0$ , the polynomial f(Y) is the zero polynomial. In particular, its constant term is zero and we have that for  $j = \{1, \ldots, M\}$ 

$$c_{jg^{\alpha x}} = a_{jg^{\alpha x}}, c_{jg^{\alpha x^{n+1}}} = 1, c_{jg^{\alpha x^{n}}} = c_{jg^{\alpha x^{2n+1}}},$$

for i = 2, ..., 2n + 1

$$c_{jq^{\alpha x^i}} = c_{jq^{\alpha x^{i-1}}} a_{jq^{\alpha x^i}}$$
 .

Combining, we get that

<span id="page-56-0"></span>
$$\prod_{i=1}^{n} a_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} = \prod_{i=n+2}^{2n+1} a_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}}.$$
 (28)

We also have that

$$e(g^{\alpha a_{j,n+1}x^{n+1}}U_j,h)e(V_j,h^{x^{n+1}}) = e(A_j,h)$$

Using that for j = 1, ..., M,

$$\begin{split} & \mathsf{EqHelper}_1(X, \left[U_i\right], \left[V_i\right], \left[A_i\right], a_{i,n+1}, n) = \bot \;, \\ & \mathsf{EqHelper}_2(X, x, \alpha, \left[U_i\right], \left[V_i\right], \left[A_i\right], a_{i,n+1}, n) = \bot \;, \\ & \mathsf{EqHelper}_3(X, x, \left[U_i\right], \left[V_i\right], \left[A_i\right], a_{i,n+1}) = \bot \;, \end{split}$$

we can show that

$$a_{jg^{\alpha x^i}} = \begin{cases} u_{jg^{\alpha x^i}} & \text{ for } 1 \leqslant i \leqslant n \\ v_{jq^{\alpha x^i - n - 1}} & \text{ for } n + 2 \leqslant i \leqslant 2n + 1 \end{cases} \;.$$

Combining with (28) we have that

$$\prod_{i=1}^n u_{jg^{\alpha x^i}} = \prod_{i=1}^n v_{jg^{\alpha x^i}} .$$

Now from the definition of  $U_j, V_j$  we have that  $u_{jg^{\alpha x^i}} = \alpha s_{jg^{\alpha x^i}} x^i + \beta_j \alpha \sigma_{j,i} x^i + \gamma_j \alpha x^i$  and  $v_{jg^{\alpha x^i}} = \alpha s'_{\sigma^{\alpha x^i}} x^i + \beta \alpha i x^i + \gamma_j \alpha x^i$ . Therefore,

$$\prod_{i=1}^{n} \left( \alpha s_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} x^{i} + \beta_{j} \alpha \sigma_{j,i} x^{i} + \gamma_{j} \alpha x^{i} \right) = \prod_{i=1}^{n} \left( \alpha s'_{g^{\alpha x^{i}}} x^{i} + \beta \alpha i x^{i} + \gamma_{j} \alpha x^{i} \right)$$

Simplifying we get,

$$\prod_{i=1}^{n} \left( s_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} + \beta_{j} \sigma_{j,i} + \gamma_{j} \right) = \prod_{i=1}^{n} \left( s'_{jg^{\alpha x^{i}}} + \beta_{j} i + \gamma_{j} \right)$$

Since  $\tau|_{(\beta_j,\gamma_j)} \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}^{\mathsf{SnACSPf}}$ , we have that  $(\beta_j,\gamma_j) \notin \mathsf{BadCh}(\tau|_{(\beta_j,\gamma_j)})$ . Therefore,  $\mathsf{SZ}(f(\mathsf{B},\varGamma),(\beta_j,\gamma_j))$  is false where f is as defined in  $\mathsf{CheckBad}(\tau',(\beta_j,\gamma_j))$ . Since we have here that  $f(\beta_j,\gamma_j)=0$ , the polynomial  $f(\mathsf{B},\varGamma)$  is the zero polynomial. Hence we have that for  $j=\{1,\ldots,M\}$ 

$$s_{jg^{\alpha x^i}} = s_{jg^{\alpha x^{\sigma_i}}} \ .$$

Additionally we can infer the following from the opening of the commitments  $W'_j, Q'_j$  (similar to how we derived the value for a above)

$$v_j = \left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d \delta_j^i s_{g^{\alpha x^i}}'\right), v_j = \left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d (\delta_j y_j)^i \psi_i\right).$$

Equating the two values of  $v_i$  we get that

$$\left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^{d} \delta_j^i s_{g^{\alpha x^i}}'\right) = \left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^{d} (\delta_j y_j)^i \psi_i\right).$$

Since  $\tau|_{\delta_j} \notin \mathcal{T}_{\mathsf{BadCh}}^{\mathsf{SnACSPf}}$ , we have that  $\delta_j \notin \mathsf{BadCh}(\tau|_{\delta_j})$ . Therefore,  $\mathsf{SZ}(f(\Delta), \delta_j)$  is false where f is as defined in  $\mathsf{CheckBad}(\tau', \delta_j)$ . Since we have here that  $f(\delta_j) = 0$ , the polynomial f(Y) is the zero polynomial. In particular, its constant term is zero and we have that for  $j = \{1, \ldots, M\}$ 

$$s'_{ia^{\alpha x^i}} = \psi_i y^i \text{ for } i = 1, \dots, n$$
,

and  $s'_{jq^{\alpha x^i}}=0$  for i<=0 and i>n. Since we derived  $s_{jg^{\alpha x^i}}=s_{jg^{\alpha x^{\sigma_i}}}$  above, we have that

$$s_{iq^{\alpha x^i}} = \psi_{\sigma_i} y^{\sigma_i} ,$$

and  $s_{jg^{\alpha x^i}} = 0$  for  $i \le 0$  and i > n. Additionally we can infer the following from the opening of the commitment  $W_i$  (similar to how we derived the value for a above)

$$s_j = \left(\sum_{\substack{i=-d\\i\neq 0}}^d z^i s_{jg^{\alpha x^i}}\right).$$

Plugging in the values of  $s_{ia^{\alpha x^i}}$ 

$$s_j = \left(\sum_{i=1}^n z^i \psi_{\sigma_i} y^{\sigma_i}\right) .$$

Since  $s(X,Y) = \sum_{j=1}^{M} \sum_{i=1}^{n} X^{i} \psi_{\sigma_{j,i}} Y^{\sigma_{j,i}}$ , we have that  $s = \sum_{i=1}^{M} s_i = s(z,y)$ . So, we have that

$$t = a(b + s(z, y)) - k(y).$$

Plugging the values of a, b, t, s(z, y) we get that

$$\begin{pmatrix} \sum_{i=-d \ i\neq 0}^d z^i t_{g^{\alpha x^i}} \end{pmatrix} = \begin{pmatrix} \sum_{i=n-2d \ i\neq n-d}^n z^i r_{g^{\alpha x^i-n+d}} \end{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \sum_{i=n-2d \ i\neq n-d}^n (yz)^i r_{g^{\alpha x^i-n+d}} + s(z,y) \\ -k(y) \end{pmatrix}$$

Since  $\tau|_z \notin \mathcal{T}^{\sf SnACSPf}_{\sf BadCh}$ , we have that  $z \notin \sf BadCh(\tau|_z)$ . Therefore,  $\sf SZ}(f(Z),z)$  is false where f is as defined in  $\sf CheckBad(\tau',z)$ . Since we have here that f(z)=0, the polynomial f(Z) must

```

                                                                                                                                                       Oracle O<sup>1</sup><sub>ext</sub> (\tau = (a_1, c_1, ..., a_{i-1}, c_{i-1}), a_i):
```
